The schema is given below:\\n47:  *\\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\\n50:  *  Length => Int32\\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\\n66:  *\\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\\n86:  *\\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\\n98:  *\\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n102:  */\\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends The schema is given below:\\n47:  *\\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\\n50:  *  Length => Int32\\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\\n66:  *\\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\\n86:  *\\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\\n98:  *\\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n102:  */\\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\\n104:     static final int BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET = 0;\\n105:     static final int BASE_OFFSET_LENGTH = 8;\\n106:     static final int LENGTH_OFFSET = static final int MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET = BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET + BASE_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH;\\n121:     static final int MAX_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH = 8;\\n122:     static final int PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET = The schema is given below:\n47:  *\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\n50:  *  Length => Int32\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\n63:  *\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\n66:  *\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n72:  *\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\n81:  *\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\n86:  *\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\n91:  *\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n96:  *\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\n98:  *\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n102:  */\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch             bufferOutputStream, deleteHorizonMs)) {\\n185:                         MemoryRecords records = builder.build();\\n186:                         int filteredBatchSize = records.sizeInBytes();\\n187:                         MemoryRecordsBuilder.RecordsInfo info = builder.info();\\n188:                         filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(info.maxTimestamp, info.shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp,\\n189:                             maxOffset, retainedRecords.size(), filteredBatchSize);\\n190:                     }\\n191:                 }\\n192:             } else if (batchRetention == BatchRetention.RETAIN_EMPTY) {\\n193:                 if (batch.magic() < RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2) // should never happen\\n194:                     throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"Empty batches are only supported for magic v2 and above\\\");\\n195: \\n196:                 bufferOutputStream.ensureRemaining(DefaultRecordBatch.RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD);\\n197:                 DefaultRecordBatch.writeEmptyHeader(bufferOutputStream.buffer(), RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, batch.producerId(),\\n198:                         batch.producerEpoch(), batch.baseSequence(), batch.baseOffset(), batch.lastOffset(),\\n199:                         batch.partitionLeaderEpoch(), batch.timestampType(), batch.maxTimestamp(),\\n200:                         batch.isTransactional(), batch.isControlBatch());\\n201:                 filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(batch, 0, true);\\n202:             }\\n203: \\n204:             // If we had to allocate a new buffer to fit the filtered buffer (see KAFKA-5316), return early to\\n205:             // avoid the need for additional allocations.\\n206:             ByteBuffer outputBuffer = bufferOutputStream.buffer();\\n207:             if (outputBuffer != destinationBuffer) {\\n208:                 filterResult.outputBuffer = outputBuffer;\\n209:                 return filterResult;\\n210:             }\\n211:         }\\n212: \\n213:         return filterResult;\\n214:     }\\n215: \\n216:     private static BatchFilterResult filterBatch(RecordBatch batch,\\n217:                                                  BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier,\\n218:                                                  FilterResult filterResult,\\n219:                                                  RecordFilter filter) {\\n220:         try (final CloseableIterator<Record> iterator = batch.streamingIterator(decompressionBufferSupplier)) {\\n221:             long maxOffset = -1;\\n222:             boolean containsTombstones = false;\\n223:             // Convert records with old record versions\\n224:             boolean writeOriginalBatch = batch.magic() >= RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE;\\n225:             List<Record> retainedRecords = new ArrayList<>();\\n226:             while (iterator.hasNext()) {\\n227:                 Record record = iterator.next();\\n228:                 filterResult.messagesRead += 1;\\n229: \\n230:                 if (filter.shouldRetainRecord(batch, record)) {\\n231:                     if (record.offset() > maxOffset)\\n232:                         maxOffset = record.offset();\\n233: \\n234:                     retainedRecords.add(record);\\n235: \\n236:                     if (!record.hasValue()) {\\n237:                         containsTombstones = true;\\n238:                     }\\n239:                 } else {\\n240:                     writeOriginalBatch = false;\\n241:                 }\\n242:             }\\n243:             return new BatchFilterResult(retainedRecords, writeOriginalBatch, containsTombstones, maxOffset);\\n244:         }\\n245:     }\\n246: \\n247:     private static class BatchFilterResult {\\n248:         private final List<Record> retainedRecords;\\n249:         private final boolean writeOriginalBatch;\\n250:         private final boolean containsTombstones;\\n251:         private final long maxOffset;\\n252:         private BatchFilterResult(List<Record> retainedRecords,\\n253:                                   final boolean writeOriginalBatch,\\n254:                                   final boolean containsTombstones,\\n255:                                   final long maxOffset) {\\n256:             this.retainedRecords = retainedRecords;\\n257:             this.writeOriginalBatch = writeOriginalBatch;\\n258:             this.containsTombstones = containsTombstones;\\n259:             this.maxOffset = maxOffset;\\n260:         }\\n261:     }\\n262: \\n263:     private static MemoryRecordsBuilder buildRetainedRecordsInto(RecordBatch originalBatch,\\n264:                                                                  List<Record> retainedRecords,\\n265:                                                                  ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream,\\n266:                                                                  final long deleteHorizonMs) {\\n267:         Compression compression = Compression.of(originalBatch.compressionType()).build();\\n268:         // V0 has no timestamp type or timestamp, so we set the timestamp to CREATE_TIME and timestamp to NO_TIMESTAMP.\\n269:         // Note that this differs from produce up-conversion where the timestamp type topic config is used and the log append\\n270:         // time is generated if the config is LOG_APPEND_TIME. The reason for the different behavior is that there is\\n271:         // no appropriate log append time we can generate at compaction time.\\n272:         TimestampType timestampType = originalBatch.timestampType() == TimestampType.NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE ?\\n273:                 TimestampType.CREATE_TIME : originalBatch.timestampType();\\n274:         long logAppendTime = timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME ?\\n275:                 originalBatch.maxTimestamp() : RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\\n276:         long baseOffset = originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2 ?\\n277:                 originalBatch.baseOffset() : retainedRecords.get(0).offset();\\n278: \\n279:         // Convert records with older record versions to the current one\\n280:         MemoryRecordsBuilder builder = new MemoryRecordsBuilder(bufferOutputStream, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE,\\n281:                 compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime, originalBatch.producerId(),\\n282:                 originalBatch.producerEpoch(), originalBatch.baseSequence(), originalBatch.isTransactional(),\\n283:                 originalBatch.isControlBatch(), originalBatch.partitionLeaderEpoch(), bufferOutputStream.limit(), deleteHorizonMs);\\n284: \\n285:         for (Record record : retainedRecords)\\n286:             builder.append(record);\\n287: \\n288:         if (originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2)\\n289:             // we must preserve the last offset from the initial batch in order to ensure that the\\n290:             // last sequence number from the batch remains even after compaction. Otherwise, the producer\\n291:             // could incorrectly see an out of sequence error.\\n292:             builder.overrideLastOffset(originalBatch.lastOffset());\\n293: \\n294:         return builder;\\n295:     }\\n296: \\n297:     /**\\n298:      * Get the byte buffer that backs this instance for reading.\\n299:      */\\n300:     public ByteBuffer buffer() {\\n301:         return buffer.duplicate();\\n302:     }\\n303: \\n304:     @Override\\n305:     public MemoryRecords slice(int position, int size) {\\n306:         if (position < 0)\\n307:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid position: \\\" + position + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n308:         if (position > buffer.limit())\\n309:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Slice from position \\\" + position + \\\" exceeds end position of \\\" + this);\\n310:         if (size < 0)\\n311:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid size: \\\" + size + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n312: \\n313:         int availableBytes = Math.min(size, buffer.limit() - position);\\n314:         // As of now, clients module support Java11 hence can't use ByteBuffer::slice(position, size) method.\\n315:         // So we need to create a duplicate buffer and set the position and limit. Duplicate buffer\\n316:         // is backed by original bytes hence not the content but only the relative position and limit\\n317:         // are changed in the duplicate buffer. Once the position and limit are set, we can call the\\n318:         // slice method to get the sliced buffer, which is a backed by the original buffer with the\\n319:         // position reset to 0 and limit set to the size of the slice.\\n320:         ByteBuffer slicedBuffer = buffer.duplicate();\\n321:         slicedBuffer.position(position);\\n322:         slicedBuffer.limit(position + availableBytes);\\n323:         // Reset the position to 0 so that the sliced view has a relative position.\\n324:         slicedBuffer = slicedBuffer.slice();\\n325: \\n326:         return readableRecords(slicedBuffer);\\n327:     }\\n328: \\n329:     @Override\\n330:     public Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches() {\\n331:         return batches;\\n332:     }\\n333: \\n334: \\\")\\\";\\n339:     }\\n340: \\n341:     @Override\\n342:     public boolean equals(Object o) {\\n343:         if (this == o)\\n344:             return true;\\n345:         if (o == null || }\\n352: \\n353:     @Override\\n354:     public int hashCode() {\\n355:         return buffer.hashCode();\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     public abstract static class RecordFilter {\\n359: See the NOTICE file distributed with\n * this work for additional information regarding copyright ownership.\n * The ASF licenses this file to You under the Apache License, Version 2.0\n * (the \"License\"); you may not use this file except in compliance with\n * the License. You may obtain a copy of the License at\n *\n *    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n *\n * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n * distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n * limitations under the License.\n */\npackage org.apache.kafka.common.record.internal;\n\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.BufferSupplier;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.CloseableIterator;\n\nimport java.nio.ByteBuffer;\nimport java.util.Iterator;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.OptionalLong;\n\n/**\n * A {@code RecordBatch} is a container for one or more {@link Record} objects as defined by the\n * Kafka binary wire protocol. It is the fundamental unit of data transfer between producers,\n * brokers, and consumers.\n *\n * <p>The batch format has evolved over three major versions, identified by the {@link #magic()} byte:\n * <ul>\n *   <li><b>Magic v0</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V0}): Legacy format. A batch always contains exactly\n *       one record when uncompressed; multiple records are allowed only under compression.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v1</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V1}): Adds per-record timestamps. Same single-record\n *       constraint as v0 when uncompressed.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v2</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V2}) and above: Current format. Batches generally\n *       contain multiple records regardless of compression. Adds idempotent producer support\n *       (producer id, epoch, sequence numbers) and transactional semantics.</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * <p>Instances of this interface are obtained by iterating over a {@link Records} object (e.g.\n * {@link MemoryRecords} or {@code FileRecords}) via {@link Records#batches()}. They provide\n * shallow access to batch-level metadata (offsets, timestamps, producer identity, compression) as\n * well as deep access to the individual {@link Record} objects contained within.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> Implementations of this interface are <em>not</em> thread-safe.\n * External synchronisation is required when a single batch instance is accessed concurrently from\n * multiple threads. In practice, batches are short-lived objects consumed on a single thread\n * during fetch or log-append operations.\n *\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see DefaultRecordBatch\n * @see Record\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n\n    /**\n     * The \"magic\" values\n     */\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V0 = 0;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V1 = 1;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V2 = 2;\n\n    /**\n     * The current \"magic\" value\n     */\n    byte CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE = MAGIC_VALUE_V2;\n\n    /**\n     * Timestamp value for records without a timestamp\n     */\n    long NO_TIMESTAMP = -1L;\n\n    /**\n     * Values used in the v2 record format by non-idempotent/non-transactional producers or when\n     * up-converting from an older format.\n     */\n    long NO_PRODUCER_ID = -1L;\n    short NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH = -1;\n    int NO_SEQUENCE = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Used to indicate an unknown leader epoch, which will be the case when the record set is\n     * first created by the producer.\n     */\n    int NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the checksum of this batch is correct.\n     *\n     * @return true If so, false otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Raise an exception if the checksum is not valid.\n     *\n     * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.CorruptRecordException if the batch checksum does not\n     *         match the recomputed value, indicating data corruption\n     */\n    void ensureValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the checksum of this record batch, which covers the batch header as well as all of the records.\n     *\n     * @return The 4-byte unsigned checksum represented as a long\n     */\n    long checksum();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the max timestamp or log append time of this record batch.\n     *\n     * If the timestamp type is create time, this is the max timestamp among all records contained in this batch and\n     * the value is updated during compaction.\n     *\n     * @return The max timestamp\n     */\n    long maxTimestamp();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the timestamp type of this record batch. This will be {@link TimestampType#NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE}\n     * if the batch has magic 0.\n     *\n     * @return The timestamp type\n     */\n    TimestampType timestampType();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the base offset contained in this record batch. For magic version prior to 2, the base offset will\n     * always be the offset of the first message in the batch. This generally requires deep iteration and will\n     * return the offset of the first record in the record batch. For magic version 2 and above, this will return\n     * the first offset of the original record batch (i.e. prior to compaction). For non-compacted topics, the\n     * behavior is equivalent.\n     *\n     * Because this requires deep iteration for older magic versions, this method should be used with\n     * caution. Generally {@link #lastOffset()} is safer since access is efficient for all magic versions.\n     *\n     * @return The base offset of this record batch (which may or may not be the offset of the first record\n     *         as described above).\n     */\n    long baseOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the last offset in this record batch (inclusive). If the message format does not support streaming\n     * iteration, then the normal iterator is returned. Either way, callers should ensure that the iterator is closed.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> For compressed batches, this iterator decompresses records lazily on demand,\n     * avoiding the need to allocate memory for all decompressed records up-front. Reusing the\n     * {@link BufferSupplier}-supplied buffers across calls (e.g. via a thread-local pool) can\n     * significantly reduce GC pressure, especially for large batches or high-throughput consumers.\n     *\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported.\n     *                                    For small record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4)\n     *                                    will dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n     *                                    batch. As such, a supplier that reuses buffers will have a significant\n     *                                    performance impact.\n     * @return The closeable iterator\n     */\n    CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this is a control batch (i.e. whether the control bit is set in the batch attributes).\n     * For magic versions prior to 2, this is always false.\n     *\n     * @return Whether this is a batch containing control records\n     */\n    boolean isControlBatch();\n\n    /**\n     * Iterate all records to find the offset of the record with the maximum timestamp.\n     *\n     * <p>Notes:\n     * <ol>\n     *   <li>If multiple records share the same maximum timestamp, the offset of the earliest such\n     *       record is returned.</li>\n     *   <li>Always returns {@link Optional#empty()} when {@link #magic()} equals\n     *       {@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V0}, because v0 batches carry no per-record timestamps.</li>\n     * </ol>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This default implementation performs a full scan of all records\n     * via {@link #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)}, including decompression for compressed\n     * batches. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01FavTqFdfGJoHynpvBNsVxR","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01QNhmQvPU9ri48ZycVAuost","name":"Write","input":{"path":"/workspace/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/internal/DefaultRecordBatch.java","content":"/*\n * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n * contributor license agreements. This class provides both read and\n * in-place-mutation access to a single batch encoded in the Kafka binary wire format. The on-wire\n * schema is:\n *\n * <pre>\n * RecordBatch =&gt;\n *   BaseOffset            =&gt; Int64\n *   Length                =&gt; Int32\n *   PartitionLeaderEpoch  =&gt; Int32\n *   Magic                 =&gt; Int8\n *   CRC                   =&gt; Uint32\n *   Attributes            =&gt; Int16\n *   LastOffsetDelta       =&gt; Int32  // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n *   BaseTimestamp         =&gt; Int64\n *   MaxTimestamp          =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerId            =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerEpoch         =&gt; Int16\n *   BaseSequence          =&gt; Int32\n *   RecordsCount          =&gt; Int32\n *   Records               =&gt; [Record]\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p>When compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n * directly following the count of the number of records.\n *\n * <p>The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that\n * follow the CRC). It is located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the\n * magic byte before deciding how to interpret the bytes between the batch length and the magic\n * byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC computation to avoid the need\n * to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by the broker.\n * The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction:</b> Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first\n * and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is\n * required in order to be able to restore the producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did\n * not retain the last sequence number, then following a partition leader failure, once the new\n * leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence expected number would no\n * longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an unexpected\n * {@code OutOfOrderSequence} error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be\n * preserved for duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by\n * verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that\n * producer.\n *\n * <p>Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may\n * still retain an empty batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as\n * described above. These empty batches are retained only until either a new sequence number is\n * written by the corresponding producer or the producerId is expired from lack of activity.\n *\n * <p>There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction.\n * The {@code BaseTimestamp} field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the\n * batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to\n * {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP}. If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the\n * {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction\n * markers in the batch should be removed.\n *\n * <p>Similarly, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current\n * records if the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME}. For\n * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, on the other hand, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field\n * reflects the timestamp set by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the\n * {@code MaxTimestamp} of an empty batch always retains the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n *\n * <p>The current attributes bit layout:\n * <pre>\n *  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n *  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> This class is <em>not</em> thread-safe. The underlying\n * {@link ByteBuffer} is accessed without synchronisation. Concurrent reads or any combination of\n * reads and in-place mutations (e.g. {@link #setLastOffset}, {@link #setMaxTimestamp},\n * {@link #setPartitionLeaderEpoch}) from multiple threads requires external synchronisation.\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n    static final int BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET = 0;\n    static final int BASE_OFFSET_LENGTH = 8;\n    static final int LENGTH_OFFSET = BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET + BASE_OFFSET_LENGTH;\n    static final int      int baseSequence = baseSequence();\n        if (baseSequence == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\n            return RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE;\n        return incrementSequence(baseSequence, lastOffsetDelta());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CompressionType compressionType() {\n        return CompressionType.forId(attributes() & COMPRESSION_CODEC_MASK);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int sizeInBytes() {\n        return LOG_OVERHEAD + buffer.getInt(LENGTH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    private int count() {\n        return buffer.getInt(RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Integer countOrNull() {\n        return count();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void writeTo(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        buffer.put(this.buffer.duplicate());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void writeTo(ByteBufferOutputStream outputStream) {\n        outputStream.write(this.buffer.duplicate());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean isTransactional() {\n        return (attributes() & TRANSACTIONAL_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    private boolean hasDeleteHorizonMs() {\n        return (attributes() & DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public OptionalLong deleteHorizonMs() {\n        if (hasDeleteHorizonMs())\n            return OptionalLong.of(buffer.getLong(BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET));\n        else\n            return OptionalLong.empty();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean isControlBatch() {\n        return (attributes() & CONTROL_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int partitionLeaderEpoch() {\n        return buffer.getInt(PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Returns an {@link InputStream} that reads the raw (possibly compressed) record bytes of this\n     * batch, starting immediately after the fixed batch header.\n     *\n     * <p>If compression is enabled, the stream transparently wraps the underlying buffer bytes with\n     * the Callers must close the stream after use to release that buffer back\n     * to the supplier pool.\n     *\n     * @param bufferSupplier supplier of temporary decompression buffers; must not be {@code buffer = this.buffer.duplicate();\n        buffer.position(RECORDS_OFFSET);\n        return Compression.of(compressionType()).build().wrapForInput(buffer, magic(), bufferSupplier);\n    }\n\n    private CloseableIterator<Record> compressedIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier, boolean skipKeyValue) {\n        final InputStream inputStream = recordInputStream(bufferSupplier);\n\n        if (skipKeyValue) {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readPartiallyFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        } else {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        }\n    }\n\n    private CloseableIterator<Record> uncompressedIterator() {\n        final ByteBuffer buffer = this.buffer.duplicate();\n        buffer.position(RECORDS_OFFSET);\n        return new RecordIterator() {\n            @Override\n            protected Record readNext(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) {\n                try {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(buffer, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                } catch (BufferUnderflowException e) {\n                    throw new InvalidRecordException(\"Incorrect declared batch size, premature EOF reached\");\n                }\n            }\n uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // for a normal iterator, we cannot ensure that the underlying compression stream is closed,\n        // so we decompress the full record set here. Use cases which call for a lower memory footprint\n        // can use `streamingIterator` at the cost of additional complexity\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iterator = compressedIterator(BufferSupplier.NO_CACHING, false)) {\n            List<Record> records = new ArrayList<>(count());\n            while (iterator.hasNext())\n                records.add(iterator.next());\n            return records.iterator();\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> skipKeyValueIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (count() == 0) {\n            return CloseableIterator.wrap(Collections.emptyIterator());\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * For uncompressed iterator, it is actually not worth skipping key / value / headers at all since\n         * its ByteBufferInputStream's skip() function is less efficient compared with just reading it actually\n         * as it will allocate new byte array.\n         */\n        if (!isCompressed())\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // we define this to be a closable iterator so that caller (i.e. the log validator) needs to close it\n        // while we can save memory footprint of not decompressing the full record set ahead of time\n        return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, true);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (isCompressed())\n            return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, false);\n        else\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setLastOffset(long offset) {\n        buffer.putLong(BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, offset - lastOffsetDelta());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n        long currentMaxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        // We don't need to recompute crc if the timestamp is not updated.\n        if (timestampType() == timestampType && currentMaxTimestamp == maxTimestamp)\n            return;\n\n        byte attributes = computeAttributes(compressionType(), timestampType, isTransactional(), isControlBatch(), hasDeleteHorizonMs());\n        buffer.putShort(ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, attributes);\n        buffer.putLong(MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, maxTimestamp);\n        long crc = computeChecksum();\n        ByteUtils.writeUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET, crc);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setPartitionLeaderEpoch(int epoch) {\n        buffer.putInt(PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, epoch);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long checksum() {\n        return ByteUtils.readUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    public boolean isValid() {\n        return sizeInBytes() >= RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD && checksum() == computeChecksum();\n    }\n\n    private long computeChecksum() {\n        return Crc32C.compute(buffer, ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, buffer.limit() - TRANSACTIONAL_FLAG_MASK : 0;\n        if (isControl)\n            attributes |= CONTROL_FLAG_MASK;\n        if (type.id > 0)\n            attributes |= (byte) (COMPRESSION_CODEC_MASK & type.id);\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            attributes |= TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK;\n        if (isDeleteHorizonSet)\n            attributes |= DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK;\n        return attributes;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Writes an empty (zero-record) batch header into the given buffer at its current position.\n     * This is used during log compaction to preserve producer sequence metadata when all records\n     * in a batch have been deleted.\n     *\n     * <p>The written header occupies exactly {@link #RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD} bytes. number to embed in the header\n     * @param baseOffset           the base (first) offset of the original batch\n     * @param lastOffset           the last offset of the original batch\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch the leader epoch at the time the batch was written\n     * @param timestampType        the timestamp type ({@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME} or\n     *                             {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME})\n     * @param timestamp            the timestamp to record in the header\n     * @param isTransactional      whether this batch was produced as part of a transaction\n     * @param isControlRecord      whether this batch is a control batch\n     * @see #writeHeader\n     */\n    public static void writeEmptyHeader(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                        byte magic,\n                                        long producerId,\n                                        short producerEpoch,\n                                        int                                      TimestampType timestampType,\n                                        long timestamp,\n                                        boolean isTransactional,\n                                        boolean isControlRecord) {\n        int offsetDelta = (int) (lastOffset - baseOffset);\n        writeHeader(buffer, baseOffset, offsetDelta, baseSequence, isTransactional, isControlRecord, false, partitionLeaderEpoch, 0);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Encodes a complete magic v2 batch header into the given buffer at its current position and\n     * advances the buffer position by {@link #RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD} bytes. The CRC-32C checksum\n     * covering all header fields from the attributes to the end of the declared batch size is\n     * computed and written inline.\n     *\n     * <p>This is a low-level method used by {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} during batch\n     * serialisation. Most callers should use {@link MemoryRecords#builder} or\n     * {@link #writeEmptyHeader} instead.\n     *\n     * @param buffer               the destination buffer; must have at least {@code difference between the last and base offsets in the batch\n     * @param sizeInBytes          total serialised size of the batch in bytes, including this header\n     * @param magic                the magic} is below\n     *         {@link RecordBatch#CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE} or if {@code baseTimestamp} is negative and\n     *         not equal to {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP}\n     */\n    public static void writeHeader(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                   long baseOffset,\n                                   int lastOffsetDelta,\n                                   int sizeInBytes,\n                                   byte magic,\n                                   CompressionType compressionType,\n                                   TimestampType timestampType,\n                                   long baseTimestamp,\n                                   long maxTimestamp,\n                                   long producerId,\n                                   short epoch,\n                                   int sequence,\n                                   boolean isTransactional,\n                                   boolean isControlBatch,\n                                   boolean isDeleteHorizonSet,\n                                   int partitionLeaderEpoch,\n                                   int numRecords) {\n        if (magic < RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid magic value \" + magic);\n        if (baseTimestamp < 0 && baseTimestamp != NO_TIMESTAMP)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid message timestamp \" + baseTimestamp);\n\n        short attributes = computeAttributes(compressionType, timestampType, isTransactional, isControlBatch, isDeleteHorizonSet);\n\n        int position = buffer.position();\n        buffer.putLong(position + BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, baseOffset);\n        buffer.putInt(position + LENGTH_OFFSET, sizeInBytes - LOG_OVERHEAD);\n        buffer.putInt(position + PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, partitionLeaderEpoch);\n        buffer.put(position + MAGIC_OFFSET, magic);\n        buffer.putShort(position + ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, attributes);\n        buffer.putLong(position + BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, baseTimestamp);\n        buffer.putLong(position + MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, maxTimestamp);\n        buffer.putInt(position + LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_OFFSET, lastOffsetDelta);\n        buffer.putLong(position + PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET, producerId);\n        buffer.putShort(position + PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET, epoch);\n        buffer.putInt(position + BASE_SEQUENCE_OFFSET, sequence);\n        buffer.putInt(position + RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET, numRecords);\n        long crc = Crc32C.compute(buffer, ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, sizeInBytes - ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n        buffer.putInt(position + CRC_OFFSET, (int) crc);\n        buffer.position(position + RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n all records in order to accumulate\n     * per-record sizes (including variable-length fields and varint-encoded deltas). It does not\n     * account for the overhead of any compression codec.\n     *\n     * @param baseOffset the base offset of the batch; used to compute per-record offset deltas\n     * @param records    the records whose encoded sizes should be summed; must not be {@code null}\n     * @return the total batch size in bytes (header plus all record bytes), or {@code 0} if\n     *         {@code records} is empty\n     */\n    public static int sizeInBytes(long baseOffset, Iterable<Record> records) {\n        Iterator<Record> iterator = records.iterator();\n        if (!iterator.hasNext())\n            return 0;\n\n        int size = RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD;\n        Long baseTimestamp = null;\n        while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n            Record record = iterator.next();\n            int offsetDelta = (int) (record.offset() - baseOffset);\n            if (baseTimestamp == null)\n                baseTimestamp = record.timestamp();\n            long timestampDelta = record.timestamp() - baseTimestamp;\n            size += DefaultRecord.sizeInBytes(offsetDelta, timestampDelta, record.key(), record.value(),\n                    record.headers());\n        }\n        return size;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Computes the serialised size in bytes of a magic v2 batch containing the given\n     * {@link SimpleRecord} objects, assuming sequential offset assignment starting at delta 0.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This method iterates over all records in order to accumulate\n     * per-record sizes. It does not account for the overhead of any compression codec.\n     *\n     * @param records the simple records whose encoded sizes should be summed; must not be\n     *                {@code null}\n     * @return the total batch size in bytes (header plus all record bytes), or {@code 0} if\n     *         {@code records} is empty\n     */\n    public static int sizeInBytes(Iterable<SimpleRecord> records) {\n        Iterator<SimpleRecord> iterator = records.iterator();\n        if (!iterator.hasNext())\n            return 0;\n\n        int size = RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD;\n        int offsetDelta = 0;\n        Long baseTimestamp = null;\n        while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n            SimpleRecord record = iterator.next();\n            if (baseTimestamp == null)\n                baseTimestamp = record.timestamp();\n            long timestampDelta = record.timestamp() - baseTimestamp;\n            size += DefaultRecord.sizeInBytes(offsetDelta++, timestampDelta, record.key(), record.value(),\n                    record.headers());\n        }\n        return size;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Get an upper bound on the size of a batch with only a single record using a given key and value. This method implements the wrap-around correctly so that\n     * brokers can detect duplicate and out-of-order produce requests even across sequence-number\n     * rollovers.\n     *\n     * @param sequence  the current base sequence number; must be non-negative\n     * @param increment the value to add; must be non-negative\n     * @return the resulting sequence number after incrementing, with wrap-around applied\n     * @see #decrementSequence(int, int)\n     */\n    public static int incrementSequence(int sequence, int increment) {\n        if (sequence > Integer.MAX_VALUE - increment)\n            return increment - (Integer.MAX_VALUE - sequence) - 1;\n        return sequence + increment;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decrements a producer sequence number by {@code decrement}, wrapping around at zero\n     * according to the Kafka sequence-number arithmetic.\n     *\n     * <p>This is the inverse of {@link #incrementSequence(int, int)}. decrementSequence(int sequence, int decrement) {\n        if (sequence < decrement)\n            return Integer.MAX_VALUE - (decrement - sequence) + 1;\n        return sequence - decrement;\n    }\n\n This class is used to read or\n * modify in-place an existing, already-encoded buffer of one or more {@link RecordBatch} objects.\n *\n * <p>To <em>produce</em> new record data into a fresh buffer, use {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} or\n * one of the static factory methods on this class (e.g.\n * {@link #builder(ByteBuffer, byte, Compression, TimestampType, long)},\n * {@link #withRecords}, {@link #withTransactionalRecords}, etc.).\n *\n * <p><b>Performance characteristics:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Batch metadata (offsets, sizes, timestamps) is read directly from the backing\n *       {@link ByteBuffer} without copying — access to header fields is O(1).</li>\n *   <li>Record-level access requires iterating and, for compressed batches, decompressing the\n *       record stream. Use {@link RecordBatch#streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)} with a buffer\n *       pool to minimise allocation pressure during decompression.</li>\n *   <li>{@link #validBytes()} is computed lazily on the first call and then cached; subsequent\n *       calls are O(1).</li>\n *   <li>{@link #buffer()} returns a {@link ByteBuffer#duplicate() duplicate} of the internal\n *       buffer — the position and limit of the returned view are independent of the internal\n *       buffer, but the underlying byte array is shared (copy-on-write semantics do not apply).</li>\n *   <li>{@link #slice(int, int)} similarly returns a zero-copy view over a sub-range of the\n *       backing buffer.</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> Instances of this class are <em>not</em> thread-safe. The backing\n * {@link ByteBuffer} is accessed without synchronisation. Additionally, in-place mutations\n * performed via {@link MutableRecordBatch} methods (e.g.\n * {@link MutableRecordBatch#setLastOffset setLastOffset},\n * {@link MutableRecordBatch#setMaxTimestamp setMaxTimestamp}) modify the shared buffer\n * in-place and must not race with concurrent readers. Callers that need to share a\n * {@code MemoryRecords} instance across threads must provide their own synchronisation.\n *\n * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see DefaultRecordBatch\n */\npublic class MemoryRecords extends AbstractRecords {\n    public static final MemoryRecords EMPTY = MemoryRecords.readableRecords(ByteBuffer.allocate(0));\n\n    private final ByteBuffer buffer;\n\n    private final Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches = this::batchIterator;\n\n    private int validBytes = -1;\n\n    // Construct a writable memory records\n    private MemoryRecords(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        Objects.requireNonNull(buffer, \"buffer should not be null\");\n        this.buffer = buffer;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int sizeInBytes() {\n        return buffer.limit();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int writeTo(TransferableChannel channel, int position, int length) throws IOException {\n        if (((long) position) + length > buffer.limit())\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"position+length should not be greater than buffer.limit(), position: \"\n                    + position + \", length: \" + length + \", buffer.limit(): \" + buffer.limit());\n\n        return Utils.tryWriteTo(channel, position, length, buffer);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Write all records to the given channel (including partial records).\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This method loops until every byte in the backing buffer has\n     * been written, which may require multiple {@link GatheringByteChannel#write write} calls on\n     * non-blocking channels. The internal buffer's mark/reset is used to avoid modifying the\n     * visible position of the backing buffer.\n     *\n     * @param channel The channel to write to\n     * @return The number of bytes written\n     * @throws IOException For any IO errors writing to the channel\n     */\n    public int writeFullyTo(GatheringByteChannel channel) throws IOException {\n        buffer.mark();\n        int written = 0;\n        while (written < sizeInBytes())\n            written += channel.write(buffer);\n        buffer.reset();\n        return written;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * The total number of bytes in this message set not including any partial, trailing messages. This\n     * may be smaller than what is returned by {@link #sizeInBytes()}.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> The result is computed lazily on the first call by iterating\n     * over all batches and summing their sizes. The computed value is cached; subsequent calls\n     * return the cached result in O(1).\n     *\n     * @return The number of valid bytes\n     */\n    public int validBytes() {\n        if (validBytes >= 0)\n            return validBytes;\n\n        int bytes = 0;\n        for (RecordBatch batch : batches())\n            bytes += batch.sizeInBytes();\n\n        this.validBytes = bytes;\n        return bytes;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public AbstractIterator<MutableRecordBatch> batchIterator() {\n        return new RecordBatchIterator<>(new ByteBufferLogInputStream(buffer.duplicate(), Integer.MAX_VALUE));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Validates the header of the first batch and returns batch size.\n     *\n     * @return first batch size including LOG_OVERHEAD if buffer contains header up to\n     *         magic byte, null otherwise\n     * @throws CorruptRecordException if record size or magic is invalid\n     */\n    public Integer firstBatchSize() {\n        if (buffer.remaining() < HEADER_SIZE_UP_TO_MAGIC)\n            return null;\n        return new ByteBufferLogInputStream(buffer, Integer.MAX_VALUE).nextBatchSize();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Filter the records into the provided ByteBuffer.\n     *\n     * <p>Each batch is evaluated by the supplied {@link RecordFilter}: the filter first decides\n     * at the batch level (via {@link RecordFilter#checkBatchRetention}) whether the entire batch\n     * can be dropped or must be retained; for batches that pass the batch-level check, individual\n     * records are evaluated via {@link RecordFilter#shouldRetainRecord}. Retained records are\n     * re-serialised into {@code destinationBuffer}, potentially into a new magic v2 batch if the\n     * original batch used an older format or if the delete-horizon flag needs to be set.\n     *\n     * <p>If the destination buffer runs out of space, a larger buffer is allocated automatically\n     * and returned in {@link FilterResult#outputBuffer()}. Callers should always use the buffer\n     * from {@link FilterResult#outputBuffer()} rather than the original {@code destinationBuffer}.\n     *\n     * @param filter                      The filter function\n     * @param destinationBuffer           The byte buffer to write the filtered records to\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported. For small\n     *                                    record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4) will\n     *                                    dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n     *                                    batch. As such, a supplier that reuses buffers will have a significant\n     *                                    performance impact.\n     * @return A FilterResult with a summary of the output (for metrics) timestamp of the first record)\n     * to the delete horizon of the tombstones or txn markers which are present in the batch.\n     */\n    private static FilterResult filterTo(Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches, RecordFilter filter,\n                                         ByteBuffer destinationBuffer, BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier) {\n        FilterResult filterResult = new FilterResult(destinationBuffer);\n        ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream = new ByteBufferOutputStream(destinationBuffer);\n        for (MutableRecordBatch batch : batches) {\n            final BatchRetentionResult batchRetentionResult = filter.checkBatchRetention(batch);\n            final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn = batchRetentionResult.containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n            final BatchRetention batchRetention = batchRetentionResult.batchRetention;\n\n            filterResult.bytesRead += batch.sizeInBytes();\n\n            if (batchRetention == BatchRetention.DELETE)\n                continue;\n\n            final BatchFilterResult iterationResult = filterBatch(batch, iterationResult.containsTombstones;\n            boolean writeOriginalBatch = iterationResult.writeOriginalBatch;\n            long maxOffset = iterationResult.maxOffset;\n\n            if (!retainedRecords.isEmpty()) {\n                // we check if the delete horizon should be set to a new value\n                // in which case, we need to reset the base timestamp and overwrite the containsMarkerForEmptyTxn) &&\n                    batch.deleteHorizonMs().isEmpty();\n                if (writeOriginalBatch && !needToSetDeleteHorizon) {\n                    batch.writeTo(bufferOutputStream);\n                    filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(batch, retainedRecords.size(), false);\n                } else {\n                    long       deleteHorizonMs = batch.deleteHorizonMs().orElse(RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP);\n                    try (final MemoryRecordsBuilder builder = buildRetainedRecordsInto(batch, retainedRecords,\n                            bufferOutputStream, deleteHorizonMs)) {\n                        MemoryRecords records = builder.build();\n                        int filteredBatchSize =
